## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials mechanics (constitutive modeling / thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma=stress, epsilon=strain, T=temperature) indicate a constitutive law identification problem from solid mechanics/materials science, where stress depends on deformation and temperature through elastic modulus changes, thermal expansion offsets, and thermally activated softening/hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (small-strain elastic solid with thermal expansion)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (polynomial E(T)): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varying with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) * epsilon (elastic softening with increasing temperature)
- Entropic (rubber-like) small-strain scaling: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to absolute temperature in entropic elasticity regime)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (work hardening in plastic regime; often fit on log-log)
- Elastic + nonlinear hardening mixture: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear elastic and plastic hardening contribution)
- Thermal softening applied to hardening law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (thermally activated weakening of flow stress)
- Multiplicative thermal softening (bounded): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 / (c3 + c4 * T)) (softening that saturates at high T)
- Coupled power-law in strain and temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (separable scaling used in empirical constitutive fits)
- Logarithmic strain hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + c3) (progressive hardening with diminishing returns)
- Yield-like transition with smooth saturation: sigma = c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (epsilon - c3)) (smooth elastic-to-plastic transition / yield plateau approximation)
- Thermally shifted yield/transition: sigma = c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (epsilon - (c3 + c4 * T))) (temperature shifts the strain at which yielding/transition occurs)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion offset: dependence on (epsilon - c * (T - c0)) indicates stress driven by mechanical strain after removing thermal strain.
- Elastic stiffness change with temperature: sigma proportional to epsilon with a prefactor E(T) (e.g., polynomial or exp(-c*T)) captures modulus degradation or stiffening.
- Thermal softening of flow stress: multiplicative factors like exp(-c*T) or c0/(c0 + c*T) applied to a hardening term represent reduced strength at higher T.
- Work hardening signature: sigma growing as epsilon**n (n>0) or with log(c*epsilon+c0) indicates plastic hardening with different curvature on stress–strain.
- Elastic–plastic transition: tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) or other sigmoids represent a smooth yield point/plateau rather than a sharp kink.
- Temperature-shifted transition/yield: replacing the transition location by (c0 + c1*T) models earlier yielding/softening at higher T.
- Separable scaling checks: sigma ≈ f(epsilon)*g(T) suggests multiplicative separation (e.g., epsilon**a * exp(-b*T)); strong deviations imply coupling terms like epsilon*T or T inside hardening exponents.
- Model selection for positivity/monotonicity: using exp() on modulus/strength parameters helps enforce sigma increasing with epsilon while decreasing with T when physically expected.

64.9458\,\epsilon^{0.6137}\exp\!\Big(-\frac{36.9451}{8.314\,T}\Big)\;-\;0.214822\,(T-331.684)\;+\;3.55398\,(T-331.684)\,\log(\epsilon+1).

So the GT is a sum of **three** structurally distinct parts:

1) **Product-coupled term**: \(\epsilon^{0.6137}\cdot \exp(-K/T)\) with \(K=36.9451/8.314\).

3) **Bilinear \(T\)-and-\(\log(\epsilon+1)\)** term: \(3.55398\,T\log(\epsilon+1) + \text{(const)}\cdot \log(\epsilon+1)\).

Any exactly equivalent candidate must be able (after choosing its free constants) to reproduce **(i)** an \(\exp(\text{const}/T)\) factor multiplied by a non-integer power of \(\epsilon\), and **(ii)** a term of the form \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) (not \(\epsilon\log(\cdot)\), not \(\log(T\cdot)\log(\epsilon\cdot)\), etc.), and **(iii)** a linear \(T\) term.

**GT:** `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-36.95/(8.314*T)) - 0.2148*(T - 331.68) + 3.554*(T - 331.68)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me expand the GT:
- `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T)` (since 36.95/8.314 ≈ 4.443)
- `-0.2148*T + 0.2148*331.68`
- `+3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 3.554*331.68*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T) - 0.2148*T + 71.25 + 3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1179.0*log(epsilon+1)`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` — a power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential
2. `T` — linear in T
3. Constant
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` — T times log term
5. `log(epsilon+1)` — standalone log term

Now let me check each candidate. Since epsilon ≥ 0, `|epsilon| = epsilon`.

For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce exactly these 5 basis function terms (or equivalent combinations).

Let me systematically check which candidates have the right structural components:

**Need:** `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)`, `T`, constant, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, `log(epsilon+1)`

Let me group the candidates by their terms:

**Candidate 7:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon*log(T*c4+1) + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7*exp(c8/T)*|epsilon|^c9`

The GT needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` but this has `epsilon*log(T*c4+1)` — different! Also has `exp(c6*epsilon)` instead of `log(epsilon+1)`. The term `exp(c8/T)*epsilon^c9` matches the Arrhenius term. But `epsilon*log(T*c4+1)` ≠ `T*log(epsilon+1)`. **NO MATCH**
